  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3b518bb4-9ee6-41b3-a86d-706ea081b016'

  <span id="freeText7753879806928155700" style="display:none">A paranormal thriller from Carnegie Medal winner Tim Bowler!<p> It starts with a phone call. "I'm dying," a voice tells Dusty. Who is he and how has he gotten her cell number? Dusty wants no part of this strange boy . . . until he begins saying things that only someone who knows her intimately could say things that lead her to think he knows the whereabouts of her brother, who disappeared over a year ago. Suddenly drawn in, Dusty very much wants to save this boy. Trouble is, she cannot find him. Part human, part spirit, he won't let himself be found. He is too dangerous, he says. There are mobs of people who agree and who want to see this boy dead . . . and who will hurt anyone who stands in their way.</p><p> A gripping, hair-raising mystery about a boy not of this world, and a girl determined to protect him.</p></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>  </div>

<div id="review_40195697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40195697" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/171079-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259203056p2/171079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40195697?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/171079-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/171079-jen?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40195697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9464832305531604150">I learned by reading this book that "psychological thriller" means "a book where nothing happens". There are pages and pages and pages where the only action is the main character walking down a snowy lane. The text is all vague imagery of light and snow and heat and cold and endless obsessions over the character's missing brother. There is certainly some suspense - enough to keep me going up to the bitter end, even, but by then I was skimming and speed reading just to see if the story improved b</span>
  <span id="freeText9464832305531604150" style="display:none">I learned by reading this book that "psychological thriller" means "a book where nothing happens". There are pages and pages and pages where the only action is the main character walking down a snowy lane. The text is all vague imagery of light and snow and heat and cold and endless obsessions over the character's missing brother. There is certainly some suspense - enough to keep me going up to the bitter end, even, but by then I was skimming and speed reading just to see if the story improved by the ending. It didn't. <br /><br />Another thing I learned by reading this book: apparently teenagers can't spell to save their lives when sending text messages. I get that you use a lot of abbreviated lingo when texting, but some of the exchanges made the characters sound like morons. Not sure if this is meant to be an indictment on public education, or if the author really thinks 15-year-olds are that stupid, but either way it was distracting from the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9464832305531604150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955163442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11884040843090495573">I have questions. Many questions.<br/><br/>That's the thing - this book leaves things pretty open-ended, and the reveal you do get doesn't come until the very end.<br/><br/>The main character was a little hard to relate to throughout. I didn't really understand why she just kept lying to everybody and keeping secrets that didn't seem to matter much and would only pull her into more trouble. I felt like there was some unnecessary drama as well, especially on her part.<br/><br/>The writing was pretty good; it definitely gave m</span>
  <span id="freeText11884040843090495573" style="display:none">I have questions. Many questions.<br /><br />That's the thing - this book leaves things pretty open-ended, and the reveal you do get doesn't come until the very end.<br /><br />The main character was a little hard to relate to throughout. I didn't really understand why she just kept lying to everybody and keeping secrets that didn't seem to matter much and would only pull her into more trouble. I felt like there was some unnecessary drama as well, especially on her part.<br /><br />The writing was pretty good; it definitely gave me chills, and the book was extremely captivating. <b>I honestly don't feel completely happy with my rating of 3 stars - it seems too low.</b> But 4 stars also seems wayyyyy too high.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13200422?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/796384-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192727152" href="/book/show/824498.Frozen_Fire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13200422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2524212145909955942">The first page sucked me right in. Dusty, sitting alone in her house, far from any neighbors, receives a phone call from a mysterious boy who has just overdosed on pills and wants to hear a comforting voice as he slips into death. As they talk, the boy lets slip details that convince Dusty he knows what happened to her brother, Josh, who disappeared two years ago. In a panic, Dusty races out into a snow storm to find the boy and a clue to finding Josh.<br/><br/>Bowler creates a taut, atmospheric thriller </span>
  <span id="freeText2524212145909955942" style="display:none">The first page sucked me right in. Dusty, sitting alone in her house, far from any neighbors, receives a phone call from a mysterious boy who has just overdosed on pills and wants to hear a comforting voice as he slips into death. As they talk, the boy lets slip details that convince Dusty he knows what happened to her brother, Josh, who disappeared two years ago. In a panic, Dusty races out into a snow storm to find the boy and a clue to finding Josh.<br /><br />Bowler creates a taut, atmospheric thriller set in a small town on the English moors. The first chapters reminded me of a horror flick, but the intensity ebbed and flowed slightly as the novel progressed (allowing me to fall asleep at night, which was a nice perk). The plot took a number of unexpected turns that kept it from turning into a Wes Craven novel. There were even - dare I say - elements of magical realism. But in a good way!<br /><br />Highly recommend it to anyone looking for an atmospheric mystery with plenty of scary chase scenes. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2524212145909955942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122500617?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=horror-dark-fantasy">horror-dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122500617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3524747184713833630">Originally posted <a href='http://guygonegeek.wordpress.com/2010/10/04/frozen-fire-by-tim-bowler/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/><i>“I’m dying,” said the voice.</i><br/><br/>This first sentence of Tim Bowler’s Frozen Fire will, right away, suck the reader in. It’s sets the ethereal and creepy atmosphere the book possess from start to end.<br/><br/>It was the beginning of the mysterious phone call Dusty received at the night of the New Year. The caller, a boy, seems to know more than what he confess — information about his missing brother or to be more accurate, information only his missing brother knows. So Dusty, although sc</span>
  <span id="freeText3524747184713833630" style="display:none">Originally posted <a href="http://guygonegeek.wordpress.com/2010/10/04/frozen-fire-by-tim-bowler/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br /><i>“I’m dying,” said the voice.</i><br /><br />This first sentence of Tim Bowler’s Frozen Fire will, right away, suck the reader in. It’s sets the ethereal and creepy atmosphere the book possess from start to end.<br /><br />It was the beginning of the mysterious phone call Dusty received at the night of the New Year. The caller, a boy, seems to know more than what he confess — information about his missing brother or to be more accurate, information only his missing brother knows. So Dusty, although scared, was determined to find this mysterious boy. This mysterious boy, as she learned, is somehow an urban legend. Rumors has it that this boy has an unnatural ability, that he looks quite inhuman and that he is accused of several crimes. The more she hear something about him, the more dangerous he seem to be and the more obsess she became to know more.<br /><br />The quality of novels like this depends on how the mystery was build up until the big reveal. Frozen Fire, I must say, kept that factor really strong. Events prior to the big reveal will keep you guessing. The big reveal itself posed more questions than answers. Readers will turn the last page finding no explanations about the boy. It was a brave move for Bowler to end it like that. A lot of readers will tend to hate the novel because of what he did. For me, however, it was a brilliant ending. It let’s your imagination to fill in the blanks, giving you the freedom to create your own version of story.<br /><br />Frozen Fire is the perfect book for under-the-blanket flashlight reading or bonfire reading. It wasn’t that scary but the uncertainties and the chain of tension-filled events will creep yourself enough. This is my first venture to Tim Bowler’s novels and it certainly won’t be the last.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3524747184713833630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_114794881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114794881" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4090986-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586127751p2/4090986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114794881?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/4090986-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=international-authors">international-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=ghosts-folklore-and-paranormal">ghosts-folklore-and-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=set-in-england-or-scotland">set-in-england-or-scotland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4090986-emily?shelf=the-2000s">the-2000s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114794881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13955592060528201715">' "I'm dying," said the voice. Dusty clutched the phone. She had no idea who this was.'<br/><br/>Well, with a hook like that who wouldn't want to keep reading? I certainly did, so much so that I bought the book...and now I wish I could give it back.<br/><br/>The main premise is a very intriguing one. A teenaged girl named Dusty recieves a midnight phone call from a strange boy who seems to know intimate details about her, most importantly the fact that her brother disappeared two years ago. <br/><br/>The setting of rural Eng</span>
  <span id="freeText13955592060528201715" style="display:none">' "I'm dying," said the voice. Dusty clutched the phone. She had no idea who this was.'<br /><br />Well, with a hook like that who wouldn't want to keep reading? I certainly did, so much so that I bought the book...and now I wish I could give it back.<br /><br />The main premise is a very intriguing one. A teenaged girl named Dusty recieves a midnight phone call from a strange boy who seems to know intimate details about her, most importantly the fact that her brother disappeared two years ago. <br /><br />The setting of rural England in winter is very important in the story and gives it a very mysterious/surreal feeling. The author spends a lot of time showing Dusty's tense relationship with her mother, who divorced her husband over the strain of their missing son. But I was so interested in learning more about the boy (who is never given a name) that I really didn't care about their relationship. Considering that Dusty spends most of the book paranoid and stressing over who the boy is, where he is and how he knows about her brother, I felt no real connection to her. There were a couple of times while reading, I just wanted her to tell someone what was going on since she was starting to stress me out. <br /><br />Ultimately, the plot just kept building and building until nothing was resolved to my satisfaction. The only mystery that is solved is what happened to Dusty's brother but I was so confused and frustrated that I didn't really care about that resolution as much. I was more intrigued by the boy and his many supernatural abilities, such as immortality. Such abilities are never fully explained and just seemed to be included as a means to make him more mysterious and strange. <br /><br />Rape is also a factor in the story but it felt more like an excuse to make the townspeople fear the boy. While one mystery is solved in regards to Dusty's brother, there were so many other loose ends that made the book very disappointing. Yes, it can be good to leave a reader wondering about the ending of a book but not so much so that they are left utterly unsatisfied when the beginning held so much promise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13955592060528201715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raychellemairee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raychellemairee" href="/user/show/3299835-raychellemairee">Raychellemairee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer90759700&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90759700" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8241031110521543452">As I read other reviews, many people didn't like this book because they didn't "understand" it and they couldn't decipher every little thing that Bowler formed into Frozen Fire. I believe that is what made this book amazing. In most books the plot it easily distributed and the end settles our heart with either understanding sadness or happiness. But not this book, oh no. Frozen Fire keeps the possibilities open so anything we can think, say, or come up with could be the reason onto why the boy e</span>
  <span id="freeText8241031110521543452" style="display:none">As I read other reviews, many people didn't like this book because they didn't "understand" it and they couldn't decipher every little thing that Bowler formed into Frozen Fire. I believe that is what made this book amazing. In most books the plot it easily distributed and the end settles our heart with either understanding sadness or happiness. But not this book, oh no. Frozen Fire keeps the possibilities open so anything we can think, say, or come up with could be the reason onto why the boy even showed up in the first place; even down to his sex. No genitals of any kind. Constantly Bowler had me trapped trying to understand and wrap my mind in the suffering the boy goes through. I wanted to reach into his mind and try to pull out what he is and what he is saying. When he'd show up so randomly in Dusty's life and speak such random words I wanted to strangle him and scream JUST SPEAK PLAIN ENGLISH but no, his simple words gave us everything we needed without being obvious and blunt.For example when he drops Dusty off by the lake after she jumps in the car with him. She constantly asks him about Josh but when he says nothing, he is saying everything. He took her to the exact spot where Josh was, lying down dead in the deep pit of the lake. The second mystery with Josh made me want to dig deeper but this writing style put up a boarder so you can only get so far inside his head and the rest is a psychological twist. I read this book slowly and I tried to force myself to make is easy, I wanted to believe that I knew everything going on was simple. But nu uh. Even now I am a lost at words to fully express my appreciation and love for authors like Bowler.<br />this book was absolutely <s>horrible</s> amazing!</span>

<div id="review_101073910" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101073910" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3072286-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415232045p2/3072286.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/3072286-beverly">Beverly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer101073910&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101073910" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4431842522861262124">I was truly excited to read this book at first because the beginning was so good. As the book went on I was looking for answers but I only became more confused. I wanted for it to have a good ending, but it didn't come!! I could not believe the ending because it answered nothing and I was so mad. I wasted my time for nothing. <br/>A few things I did not understand (and by few I mean a lot):<br/>1. Why does he not have any genitals?<br/>2. Why does he have those powers?<br/>3. Why was he following Angelica around?<br/>4.</span>
  <span id="freeText4431842522861262124" style="display:none">I was truly excited to read this book at first because the beginning was so good. As the book went on I was looking for answers but I only became more confused. I wanted for it to have a good ending, but it didn't come!! I could not believe the ending because it answered nothing and I was so mad. I wasted my time for nothing. <br />A few things I did not understand (and by few I mean a lot):<br />1. Why does he not have any genitals?<br />2. Why does he have those powers?<br />3. Why was he following Angelica around?<br />4. What did the snow-pipe thing have to do with anything?<br />5. What was with all the glowing and heat?<br />6. He had been around for at least two years already and he contacted Dusty only then? And why choose her in the first place?<br />7. Why did the van turn into a cloud, then a bird, and then a rock and then at the end the van was found underwater and footsteps were coming out of the lake? How does that even make sense? Was Dusty imagining it?<br />8. The boy seemed normal at times but other times he was so weird. Why?<br />9. Why doesn't he show up in pictures?<br />10. What happened to the boy at the end? Where did he go?<br />11. What is he??? Who is he??? Why is he there???<br /><br />I give this book three stars because it was going great up until the part where the mob gathers at Dusty's house. That's where I decided that it was over. The kid was ready to die or whatever he was planning to do without providing any explanations. Had Bowler given us at least some answers I would have given this novel a 4 or a 5, but no, he decided that it was better to leave us with a bunch of confusing events. <br />Seriously, though, I didn't understand it!! <br />If ANYONE has any answers to the above questions then please tell me because I am just so confused and disappointed. <br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349889117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer973013341205384926">Frozen Fire held just enough mystery that I wanted to read more and just a little scary that I was hesitant to. In a sense, I would call it a psych thriller and you have to be wary of these. Because sometimes they aren't good. They can be full of pages upon pages of words and still say nothing of value. Because psychs can babble if they're not good. But I felt like this one, IMO, did just enough right to keep me reading so that I could find out if Dusty would save the boy on the other end of pho</span>
  <span id="freeText973013341205384926" style="display:none">Frozen Fire held just enough mystery that I wanted to read more and just a little scary that I was hesitant to. In a sense, I would call it a psych thriller and you have to be wary of these. Because sometimes they aren't good. They can be full of pages upon pages of words and still say nothing of value. Because psychs can babble if they're not good. But I felt like this one, IMO, did just enough right to keep me reading so that I could find out if Dusty would save the boy on the other end of phone. If she would find her brother. <br /><br />Because it's a psych thriller and a mystery rolled into one a lot of scenes happen, like in a movie. She sees a swing, follows a snowy path, has conversations. Goes to the lake. Follows the boy named Josh to the car. Tries to solve the mystery, tries to find her missing brother. Dusty doesn't have wicked action fights or use magic or have a best fried to go out with and gossip about the sexiest guys in town. This book is meant to be about the mind and the deeper parts of thought, which I think people miss the point of. Or don't end up caring and then don't like the book because of. <br /><br />And that's a shame because then they think it's a bad book which it isn't. <br /><br />It isn't the best book in my bookcase but it's good enough to warrant a reread from me. And I don't regret my purchase. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9523193790545382876">Alright, here goes nothing.<br/><br/><i>"I'm dying," a voice tells Dusty. Who is he and how has he gotten her cell number? Dusty wants no part of this strange boy . . . until he begins saying things that only someone who knows her intimately could say things that lead her to think he knows the whereabouts of her brother, who disappeared over a year ago.</i><br/><br/><b>What you should do:</b><br/><br/>1. Don't tell him your real name.<br/>2. Don't admit that he has information you want.<br/>3. Don't go outside looking for him.<br/>4. Call the police pro</span>
  <span id="freeText9523193790545382876" style="display:none">Alright, here goes nothing.<br /><br /><i>"I'm dying," a voice tells Dusty. Who is he and how has he gotten her cell number? Dusty wants no part of this strange boy . . . until he begins saying things that only someone who knows her intimately could say things that lead her to think he knows the whereabouts of her brother, who disappeared over a year ago.</i><br /><br /><b>What you should do:</b><br /><br />1. Don't tell him your real name.<br />2. Don't admit that he has information you want.<br />3. Don't go outside looking for him.<br />4. Call the police pronto<br /><br /><b>What Dusty does:</b><br /><br />1. Tells him her real name.<br />2. Admits that he has information she desperately wants.<br />3. Goes outside looking for him.<br />4. Doesn't immediately call the police.<br /><br />I mean... maybe it's just me but this shit seems like common sense of exactly what NOT to do when some creepy stranger calls you and happens to somehow know a bunch of stuff about you and talks like he is watching you from outside your window.<br /><br />So from the get-go, Dusty is airing on the side of stupid.<br /><br /><b>BUT</b>, I'm not going to let the first few pages of a book determine my entire outlook on it so I keep reading. By the end, here's my conclusions:<br /><br />1. I don't know what I just read.<br /><br /><s>That's it. Review done.</s><br /><br />The second I put this book down, I forgot everything that happened. Because well, nothing happened. The beginning of the book catches you right away, it's the entire reason I bought the book 6 years ago. But after the intriguing beginning, the rest of the book just dragged. By the end, I didn't have any of the answers that I wanted and I didn't feel a connection with any of the characters, even the main character. <br /><br />By the way, who in the hell writes a book and doesn't name one of the main characters?! The name of who calls Dusty on the phone in the beginning is just never mentioned. Maybe he doesn't have a name? Maybe we're supposed to just not give a shit? I don't know. But for the love of God name your DAMN characters. <br /><br />The entire book to this day is a blur in my mind of characters I didn't care about and a story that for some reason I just couldn't follow.<br /><br />If someone came up to me and asked "<i>Lisa, what happened in the book Frozen Fire?"</i>. I'd just be like "Well sir/madam, I would <b>LOVE</b> to tell you except I HAVE NO FUCKING CLUE. I guess aliens and a missing persons case or some shit."</span>

<div id="review_507126926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/507126926" />
    <a title="Ciara T" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12827243-ciara-t"><img alt="Ciara T" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355848089p2/12827243.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/507126926?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ciara T" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ciara T" href="/user/show/12827243-ciara-t">Ciara T</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507126926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4152569389776180911">In the novel Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler, Dusty is a fifteen-year-old girl living in the United Kingdom. Living with her overprotective dad, Dusty learns to stand up for herself and to not take anything from anyone. She learned all of this when her older brother, Josh, walked out two years earlier, and her “mum” had a nervous breakdown and walked out six months after. This book is a great read, and it has action, mystery, and a teenager’s struggle to stay sane.<br/><br/>What I liked most about this book, wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4152569389776180911" style="display:none">In the novel Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler, Dusty is a fifteen-year-old girl living in the United Kingdom. Living with her overprotective dad, Dusty learns to stand up for herself and to not take anything from anyone. She learned all of this when her older brother, Josh, walked out two years earlier, and her “mum” had a nervous breakdown and walked out six months after. This book is a great read, and it has action, mystery, and a teenager’s struggle to stay sane.<br /><br />What I liked most about this book, was the fact that Bowler really gets inside the mind of a 21st century teenager, without giving away what the whole plot twist of the book is. Dusty is a very independent character, who fends for herself against bullies, people who tease her at school and her enemies, Gavin and Denny. The mysterious boy, who is still nameless and is mistaken for her older brother, is portrayed as Dusty’s secret, someone she can’t tell anyone about, or else she’d be in a world of trouble. I like the fact that Bowler describes the characters through their actions, and how they perceive things that happen to them,and how they solve the problems they’re faced with. What I didn't like about the characters was that they were all kind of muddled together, and weren't always portrayed as important as they should be.<br /><br />The plot of the book is very interesting, and is different from most books you might read. The book ends with a total plot twist, that leaves you thinking “What just happened here?”. Bowler does an excellent job of leading readers up to the conflict and climax of the book, then completely changing the book, and leading them into a direction that they didn’t expect. What happens to lead up to the conflict is Dusty being considered a suspect, and being disowned by her friends. Understanding the plot of the book will help the reader to realize what really happened when it comes at the end of the book, and is exposed through little clues throughout the entire book. The big conflict, finally finding the mystery boy, kept me interested to finish the rest of the book because I wanted to figure out what would happen to Dusty and her family.<br /><br />Using his characterization, the plot of the book, and the main conflict, Tim Bowler wrote an excellent book with an excellent theme. The main theme would be to be careful what you wish for, because you just might get it. As the reader of this book, you can learn many life lessons, and that society and the world isn't as pretty as people say it is. The genre of Frozen Fire, realistic fiction, really fits in with the big picture because it’s something that could easily happen to any one of us, with a few twists and fairy tale-like substances thrown in. I've read many books of this genre, and I plan on reading more because I like that you can relate to the genre and characters, yet you can’t because of the individual problems they face. The only negative of this genre is the fact that some of it can be too over dramatic and not seem realistic at all, which ruins the book. This book is similar to the City of Bones series I read by Cassandra Clare. They are both about people “not of this world” and are both realistic fiction. I really enjoyed that series, and would love to read her other books that continue it. If Bowler added a second book to this one, about what happens to Dusty, and what she really learns about her brother and the mystery boy.<br /><br />I awarded Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler five stars because it’s very well written, is a great book, deals with real life places and people, and is my favorite genre. This book is a must read, and I recommend everyone to read the book, because it’s very interesting, and might get you interested in more books than the type you read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4152569389776180911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_825562950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825562950" />
    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3119530-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420612320p2/3119530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/825562950?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/3119530-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=not-sure-about">not-sure-about</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=books-with-characters-i-want-to-mar">books-with-characters-i-want-to-mar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119530-kayla?shelf=covet-these-covers">covet-these-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer825562950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9183839746866813864">I picked this book up on a whim because the cover was gorgeous and intriguing and the summary had me hooked. Just as it says, so the story begins, and Dusty starts speaking to a strange boy who seems to know too much about her and claims he thought of a random phone number and it happened to connect him to her. This boy is definitely the heart and most interesting part of the story. At times the writing and plot grew bland while I waited for more news of him to surface. Oftentimes instead of the</span>
  <span id="freeText9183839746866813864" style="display:none">I picked this book up on a whim because the cover was gorgeous and intriguing and the summary had me hooked. Just as it says, so the story begins, and Dusty starts speaking to a strange boy who seems to know too much about her and claims he thought of a random phone number and it happened to connect him to her. This boy is definitely the heart and most interesting part of the story. At times the writing and plot grew bland while I waited for more news of him to surface. Oftentimes instead of the answers and actions I was looking for, more questions would pop up in the book and leave me feeling unsatisfied.<br /><br />I didn't like the way that suspense was handled in this book. While I think that the pacing was typical for mysteries of this sort, there weren't enough revelations that were full of insight or significant impact for me to justify stretching out the novel. Sometimes things felt so dull and detached from me that I didn't feel much when Dusty was in danger. I was interested but more interested in the boy and wanted to flip forward to find out more about him.<br /><br />The book ended the way I was afraid that it would because it left me almost entirely unsatisfied. Part of me could see from a higher level point of view how the ending was necessary and fit in with different elements of the story that had been set out much earlier in the tale. But I wanted more enjoyment as a reader. I wanted validation because I'd struggled through some sections of the book, waiting and hoping for answers, and I received none. I do think that I'll pick up something else by Tim Bowler and will give him another try. I'll remain disappointed in Frozen Fire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9183839746866813864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_105160069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105160069" />
    <a title="Mel (who is deeply in love with herself)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3811037-mel-who-is-deeply-in-love-with-herself"><img alt="Mel (who is deeply in love with herself)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353763955p2/3811037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105160069?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

              <span id="reviewTextContainer105160069" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13342750663740700656">This book was great. i was hooked in the moment i read the first line, which i always do when searching for new books.<br/><i>"I'm dying," said the voice.</i><br/>i mean, how can anyone not be intrigued by that stonker of a first line?<br/>the rest of the book was thought-provoking, and i found myself spellbound in the troubled world of Dusty, Josh, and the Boy, who was a fascination all by himself. <br/>Tim Bowler was great at describing the world encircling Dusty and her friends, and i have never read snow being describ</span>
  <span id="freeText13342750663740700656" style="display:none">This book was great. i was hooked in the moment i read the first line, which i always do when searching for new books.<br /><i>"I'm dying," said the voice.</i><br />i mean, how can anyone not be intrigued by that stonker of a first line?<br />the rest of the book was thought-provoking, and i found myself spellbound in the troubled world of Dusty, Josh, and the Boy, who was a fascination all by himself. <br />Tim Bowler was great at describing the world encircling Dusty and her friends, and i have never read snow being described as beautifully and majestically as Tim Bowler managed to do in this novel. absolutely stunning.<br />i must admit, i had loads of unanswered questions at the end of the novel, but i didnt dwell on them in a frustrated manner, whilst cursing Tim Bowler with every name under the sun for leaving me out of the loop; instead, i realised the story just became that much more enthralling by all the mysteries and unanswered questions clogging it up.<br /><br />the Boy was awesome, and i wish i could meet someone like him in my life, (though i doubt it would ever happen) The way he said everything Dusty and the readers needed to know in only a few words just left me stunned, and i applaud the author for creating such a mysterious, alluring character who swam around in my head all these years. (i first read this book when i was about 12 or 13, now i'm 15 and am on the hunt to buy a copy as soon as possible)<br /><br />Overall, LOVE IT!!!</span>

<div id="review_392611637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392611637" />
    <a title="Megan Houston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10500557-megan-houston"><img alt="Megan Houston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394733476p2/10500557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392611637?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Houston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Houston" href="/user/show/10500557-megan-houston">Megan Houston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392611637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14851727001126925252">I found this a really intruiging book. From the very first line of "I'm dying," it sucked you in. I liked that it was a kind of double mystery plot. There was the mysterious boy who somehow knew the protaganist, Dusty's phone number, as well as her thoughts, but there was also her missing brother Josh. As the mystery around this strange boy deepens, the plot of her brother's disappearence slowly begins to deepen to. It is definitely a book where things have to get a lot more complicated before t</span>
  <span id="freeText14851727001126925252" style="display:none">I found this a really intruiging book. From the very first line of "I'm dying," it sucked you in. I liked that it was a kind of double mystery plot. There was the mysterious boy who somehow knew the protaganist, Dusty's phone number, as well as her thoughts, but there was also her missing brother Josh. As the mystery around this strange boy deepens, the plot of her brother's disappearence slowly begins to deepen to. It is definitely a book where things have to get a lot more complicated before they can be solved. Even though the entire town is sure that this boy is a rapist and crazy, I felt myself urging Dusty to go looking for the boy, and some answers. Unlike most of the reviewers, I found Dusty very likable. The author didn't make her one of those girls who think's she's ugly and everyone else disagrees she was just a plain girl with street smarts and an aptitude for trouble as well as being known for the disappearence of her brother. She's reckless and stupid at times but you still want things to go alright for her, even if you are screaming at her for making the wrong choice. As it got closer to the end I got more and more drawn into the story and I loved the ending, as I didn't expect it. I felt that the book didn't have very much closure at the end, when it came to things such as the mob and her friends and her parents but that wasn't necessarily a bad thing and overall it was an enjoyable book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14851727001126925252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114788722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6167475555621919462">Impulse buy gone bad. I was intrigued to see what a Carnegie Medal winner could do with a psychological thriller geared for a YA audience. Sadly, not much.<br/><br/>The story dragged . . . and dragged . . . and dragged. Besides a few redundant chase scenes through the woods (I kept asking myself, haven't I read this part already? Without my Curious George bookmark, I'd have been desperately lost), and lots of agonizing internal debate on the part of the protagonist Dusty, not much happened. And yet, despi</span>
  <span id="freeText6167475555621919462" style="display:none">Impulse buy gone bad. I was intrigued to see what a Carnegie Medal winner could do with a psychological thriller geared for a YA audience. Sadly, not much.<br /><br />The story dragged . . . and dragged . . . and dragged. Besides a few redundant chase scenes through the woods (I kept asking myself, haven't I read this part already? Without my Curious George bookmark, I'd have been desperately lost), and lots of agonizing internal debate on the part of the protagonist Dusty, not much happened. And yet, despite the startling lack of action, or just plain old pacing and plot advancement, the book felt disorienting and confusing to me. This may have been because the descriptions were as redundant as the brief action scenes, or because the mysterious boy takes on a sinister edge, but never actually gets revealed for much of anything or anyone, but I felt bewildered by the time I finished. The "what did I just read?" kind of moment, followed by the "I can never get those couple of hours back" regret. You know what I mean.<br /><br />I could have been much more forgiving of this novel if so many of its flaws hadn't felt like sheer sloppiness on the part of the author. It felt like he'd rushed this book out without fully developing the plot line; I constantly felt that he had no better sense of where the story was going than I did. The dialog was stilted, and the descriptions were tired. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6167475555621919462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_71185563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71185563" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2620271-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1250517154p2/2620271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71185563?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/2620271-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780192719799" href="/book/show/824491.Frozen_Fire">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody with half a mind</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2620271-rachael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2620271-rachael?shelf=so-bad-i-feel-for-the-trees">so-bad-i-feel-for-the-trees</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2620271-rachael?shelf=avoid-at-all-costs">avoid-at-all-costs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2620271-rachael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2620271-rachael?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer71185563&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71185563" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13545811201288646584">It was dark outside. Cobweb knew this even without drawing back the curtains. It was a strange, eerie darkness which seemed to envelop her as she sat on her bed reading Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler. <br/> Her room was unusually warm for this time of year. She could hear the snow falling outside, stroking at the window, conflicting with the heat of her room. It was as if the room was a new world, a different world. It was a world separate from the frozen one that loomed outside.<br/> After glancing quickly at</span>
  <span id="freeText13545811201288646584" style="display:none">It was dark outside. Cobweb knew this even without drawing back the curtains. It was a strange, eerie darkness which seemed to envelop her as she sat on her bed reading Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler. <br /> Her room was unusually warm for this time of year. She could hear the snow falling outside, stroking at the window, conflicting with the heat of her room. It was as if the room was a new world, a different world. It was a world separate from the frozen one that loomed outside.<br /> After glancing quickly at the clock, Cobweb replaced her head within the snowy white pages of The Book. How strange it was for her to notice the inexplicably large print of this book. Surely she should be so engrossed in the novel that such trivialities become unnoticeable. But no. The thought was always there. Why?<br /> 'Why?' She murmured aloud to herself. 'Why would you make the font so large Mr Bowler? Why, when it leads to nothing but an increase in pages?'<br /> After failing to find a suitable answer, Cobweb allowed her passionate inquisition to subside. She wrapped it deep inside herself so that she could continue with this award winning novel.<br /> As she read further, flicking though the baby-font pages like a dangerously terrifying tornado, Cobweb realized with sudden terror and dread that she could not stop now. She could not abandon this book before viewing every last one of it's garbage-filled pages. <br /> 'No!' She cried in horror, throwing the book down onto the bed. But she knew it was her destiny. Cobweb could not leave this book unfinished any more than she could cease to be. It was her destiny, pulling her to the novel. After all, if she did not finish the novel, how could she review it on Good Reads? Her fate was decided. She must continue. But how Cobweb longed for a decent, well written piece of literature.<br /> 'Just a good plot, is that too much to ask for?' But there was no one to answer her but the quite moan of the wind which seemed to be agreeing with her. <br /> As she stared at the sad, unloved book sprawled across the bed, she felt a deep pity well up inside her. But it was not a pity which belonged to the author, but one which belonged to the trees which had spared their lives for it's creation.<br /> At that moment, she realized she was crying. She wiped futilely at the tears now streaking down her face.<br /> 'Those poor trees!' She wailed to herself, as dialogue is the easiest way to express such emotions. At that very moment, a fierce incandescence emanated from the book. The glow was so bright, so unfathomable 'she felt disconnected from herself, as though she were in some pocket of life detached from the world of her senses.' It was as if the book itself was a separate entity, a separate being.<br /> Momentarily frozen by sheer terror, she finally came to her senses. Slowly, slowly, slowly, slowly, she placed one hand on the corner of the illuminous book. She gripped the corner tightly with her hand and lifted the book. There, on the bed, in the exact place the book had been lay... the torch she had used to read by. Cobweb sighed, relief and sudden realization of stupidity coursing through herlike soup.<br /> Again, she made herself comfortable and continued to read, driven only by the desire to review this devilish creation. To warn all other library goers to simply run in the opposite direction of the 'B- section' of Fictional Literature. <br /> Finally, Cobweb had fulfilled her destiny. All three hundred and fifty pages of nonsense, tainting her otherwise perfect repertoire. But it was complete, although absolute bafflement still pulled at her mind. Who on earth was that boy? Why does he have these strange, unearthly powers. And, why the hell did Mr Bowler not see the importance of answering these questions? <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13545811201288646584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12375609757380697031" style="display:none">It's a late winter night when Dusty gets a phone call. She knows she can't ignore it so as she picks up the phone the voice on the other end says, "I'm Dying." Dusty wants nothing to do with this boy but it seems as if he knows everything about her brothers dissapearence. How did he know all this personal details about her life and her brother? Dusty was determined to find out. As she goes on the search for the strange boy she starts to learn more and more about him. Stories have been going around in her town about him being spotted and could be dangerous. She keeps getting phone calls from him, but how could he possibly be able to figure out her number? It gets even stranger. The stories going on about him are that he is able to do things that no normal human would be able to do.<br /><br />Rumors are going on about this boy that he is doing terrible things but Dusty knows he is not capable of doing such horibble things, but everyone else seems to think differantly. There are many people that are after Dusty because they know she has been in contact with the boy, and they don't like it! As Dusty seems to find out more and more about the strange boy, she learns more about her brother. The boy is the key to the mystery about her brother and just as she thinks she will never know the secrets of the past the boy will lead her to the answers. <br /><br />The authors purpose of writing the book is for the readers entertainment. I also believe that the reason is for the reader to learn something from the book which is the theme. The theme of the book would be that if you really want something you should try as hard as you possibly can to get it. Dusty wanted to find out the answer to her brothers dissapearence and even when the going got tough she didnt give up. <br /><br />I thought that the book was very interesting and very differant from other books I have read. I liked that the book kept me wanting to read and at the same time kept me at the edge of my seat. This book was very good so I would not change a thing about it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1669865090381966990">I recently finished reading the book Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler. This book was a young adult novel and was 272 pages long. This book was about a girl named Dusty, and the questions she has about her missing brother Josh. Her family is broken, her mom walked out on her family when her older brother Josh went missing, leaving Dusty to live with her dad. After begging her dad to finally go on a date, she has the house to herself, until a mysterious phone call from a guy she doesn't even know comes a</span>
  <span id="freeText1669865090381966990" style="display:none">I recently finished reading the book Frozen Fire by Tim Bowler. This book was a young adult novel and was 272 pages long. This book was about a girl named Dusty, and the questions she has about her missing brother Josh. Her family is broken, her mom walked out on her family when her older brother Josh went missing, leaving Dusty to live with her dad. After begging her dad to finally go on a date, she has the house to herself, until a mysterious phone call from a guy she doesn't even know comes along. This guy knows what people are feeling and thinking, but not only that, he says things only Josh says. Curious, Dusty tries to find this boy, which makes her a target for people looking for him.Soon the police and the whole town gets involved to bring this guy to justice after he was accused of some things. Dusty still wants to know what happened to Josh, so she tries to get in touch of him every chance she gets, which ultimately gets her into trouble with the police, her family, and the locals.<br /><br />This book wasn't the best book I have read by far. I started this book thinking that it was going to be more of a mystery about finding Dusty's brother, but the moment it turned supernatural it went downhill for me. I also didn't like how the book ended, it made me a bit confused about who this guy was and some other things that I wont say to keep the ending a secret. If you like supernatural creatures and some mystery this would probably be a book for you. Also I don't think I would recommend it to middle schoolers because of some of the content that was in there.The writing was pretty good and interesting. I like how its suspenseful throughout the book, which makes the book relatively quick to read. If it wasn't for the suspense and the writing style I probably would have put this book down. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12440722957175920301">In the past I tried reading this book, but never got passed the second or maybe third chapter. However this morning I woke up, made my self a cup of tea and ended up finishing the book in one sitting.<br/><br/> It starts off with a girl named Dusty, receiving a phone call from a mysterious boy.   <span id="freeText12440722957175920301" style="display:none">In the past I tried reading this book, but never got passed the second or maybe third chapter. However this morning I woke up, made my self a cup of tea and ended up finishing the book in one sitting.<br /><br /> It starts off with a girl named Dusty, receiving a phone call from a mysterious boy. The boy tells her he is dying because he over dosed, in order to kill himself. Dusty being frightened asks why he called and he tells her he just wanted someone to talk to while he slipped <i> away</i>. The boy tells her a false name and he chooses Josh. Her brothers name, who ran away a few years ago. After he hangs up she panics, thinking the boy might know something about her brothers disappearance, and if he really were to kill himself she'd want to save him. She thinks about the phone call and remembers certain sounds that bring her to the park near her house. then she finds pill bottles and foot prints in the snow. Looking further around the park the footprints disappear and then a group of three men start chasing after her and harass her. <br /><br /> After the one incident she often gets phone calls from the boy. The people start to see him around and then rumors start spreading around about the boy having raped a girl in the next town over. Her friends start avoiding her, due to the interactions with this mysterious boy.<br /><br /> Though there are parts in the book are slow and make you tired, there are also many parts that posses you, making you want more. I recommend Frozen Fire if you like stories that'll give you chills but can't exactly be considered scary. It's a thrilling and mysterious story that had me flipping the page and looking for answers.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14778665727244613515">Dusty doesn’t know anything about the boy who mysteriously calls her one night as he attempts to commit suicide, then startles her with all the personal things he knows about her and her life—like the disappearance of her brother, Josh. All she knows that there is something terribly alluring yet dangerous about him at the same time. Her curiosity drags her into an out-of-this-world intriguing mystery that makes her enemies and drives her to her tomboyish limits.<br/><br/>For there really ARE a lot of thin</span>
  <span id="freeText14778665727244613515" style="display:none">Dusty doesn’t know anything about the boy who mysteriously calls her one night as he attempts to commit suicide, then startles her with all the personal things he knows about her and her life—like the disappearance of her brother, Josh. All she knows that there is something terribly alluring yet dangerous about him at the same time. Her curiosity drags her into an out-of-this-world intriguing mystery that makes her enemies and drives her to her tomboyish limits.<br /><br />For there really ARE a lot of things strange about the boy. Like how he knows all of these intimate details about people. Or how he disappears without a trace. And then there are the stories that the angry mob from other towns tell, of the boy having a certain hold over girls and then raping them, of him disarming or killing living beings with just one wave of his hand.<br /><br />Dusty doesn’t know how to feel about this boy. Her family, the cops, her friends, the mob—all are telling her to stay away from him, she is only going to implicate herself if she continues to mess things up so that it looks like she’s helping him. But all Dusty is certain of is that the mysterious boy is the key to finding out what happened to her brother Josh, all those many years ago.<br /><br />And for that, she can’t stop getting involved, until her very life is in mortal danger.<br />FROZEN FIRE is interesting and fairly well-written. A lot happens at once, which may confuse some readers, but it is a worthwhile story, with a satisfying ending.<br /></span>

<div id="review_58341951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58341951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3172994916637935017"><i> For Dusty it started with with a phone call from a mysterious boy.<br/>At first Dusty wants nothing to do with this strange boy who has been seen lurking around Raven's Fell; but when the boy tells her something about her brother Josh, whose been missing for two years, Dusty is determined to get to the bottom of this-despite the danger of the revengeful "ponytail" man.</i><br/><br/>A physiological thriller, huh? was my first thought when I saw this at the library. I've never read one before, so I decided to try i</span>
  <span id="freeText3172994916637935017" style="display:none"><i> For Dusty it started with with a phone call from a mysterious boy.<br />At first Dusty wants nothing to do with this strange boy who has been seen lurking around Raven's Fell; but when the boy tells her something about her brother Josh, whose been missing for two years, Dusty is determined to get to the bottom of this-despite the danger of the revengeful "ponytail" man.</i><br /><br />A physiological thriller, huh? was my first thought when I saw this at the library. I've never read one before, so I decided to try it.<br />I was expecting it to be scary, but it wasn't-just weird. One thing I didn't like was Dusty's parents because they were so outa whack-guess that's why Josh turned out the way he did. There was a few bad words other than the H-E-double-tooth-pick words. Because it's set in England, most of the characters say "bloody" this or that.<br /><b> I don't recommend you read this book, though I'd say it's a pretty mild (thank-goodness) physiological thriller compared to some I've heard about.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT<br /><br />I was disappoint somewhat with the ending, not because Dusty finally found her brother (dead at the bottom of the lake) but because he did bad stuff-which probably led to drowning himself. I think the boy was either her brother's ghost coming back to tell her where he was-to put the family at ease so to say-or the boy really helped her find Josh but had no relation to him. Anyways I don't think I'll be trying any more psycho thrillers!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3172994916637935017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1298750-kyleigh?shelf=own">own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29992533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2755492081295405884">Very very very good! I about died at the ending. <br/><br/>I think I have a new favorite author. Ok, maybe not absolute fave but another great author. The suspense was killing me! I literally couldn't put it down. <br/><br/>Dusty finally got an evening to herself only to have it ruined by a mysterious boy on the phone who claims he's dying. Dusty's suddenly swept into a world of confusion where reality no longer makes sense. To make things worse the people who are hunting this mysterious boy are now after her, thin</span>
  <span id="freeText2755492081295405884" style="display:none">Very very very good! I about died at the ending. <br /><br />I think I have a new favorite author. Ok, maybe not absolute fave but another great author. The suspense was killing me! I literally couldn't put it down. <br /><br />Dusty finally got an evening to herself only to have it ruined by a mysterious boy on the phone who claims he's dying. Dusty's suddenly swept into a world of confusion where reality no longer makes sense. To make things worse the people who are hunting this mysterious boy are now after her, thinking she's harboring him. Dusty's desperate to find him, thinking that he has information on her brother who disappeared two years ago. In Dusty's desperate search for the truth, she comes to realize there are greater mysteries than than the disappearance of her brother. <br /><br />Fast paced, exciting, suspenseful and totally awesome! The one and only thing that bothered me was that you never get the big major questions answered, but on the other hand, if they were answered I don't think the book would have been nearly as fawesome! (Zaler rocks!lol) Ok... other than that reference to Peeps, this book is totally amazing and is a definite buyer! Seriously. Go. Buy. It. Now! </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RmUNSDRmZZYk9RxM2DrfILnf8PHMKiUujMuEeoyKS3bsTt4Ph2p7HrQEsElFIZhDVcCTKbOfQXjS/DMmOycLJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U5QZrzaTvPRGF/cxfqtCuhcExLYF2jmkVo2hIumK7jT5v8rohZ+ifNbmWzTjsAXZ+xunbnpvXfIIuhZ+XieuZQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer12283477390149619760">Tim Bowler is one of the UK’s most compelling and original writers for teenagers. He was born in Leigh-on-Sea and after studying Swedish at University he worked in forestry, the timber trade, teaching and translating before becoming a full-time writer. He lives with his wife in a small village in Devon and his workroom is an old stone outhouse known to friends as ‘Tim’s Bolthole’.<br/><br/>Tim has written t</span>
  <span id="freeText12283477390149619760" style="display:none">Tim Bowler is one of the UK’s most compelling and original writers for teenagers. He was born in Leigh-on-Sea and after studying Swedish at University he worked in forestry, the timber trade, teaching and translating before becoming a full-time writer. He lives with his wife in a small village in Devon and his workroom is an old stone outhouse known to friends as ‘Tim’s Bolthole’.<br /><br />Tim has written twenty books and won fifteen awards, including the prestigious Carnegie Medal for River Boy. His most recent novel is the gripping Bloodchild and his provocative Blade series is being hailed as a groundbreaking work of fiction. He has been described by the Sunday Telegraph as ‘the master of the psychological thriller’ and by the Independent as ‘one of the truly individual voices in British teenage fiction’.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12283477390149619760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
